        The forest’s thickness is lessening,
      with room for paths of turned earth,
  rectangular pits, a whiteness as of mushrooms
             peeping from the ground.
With horror we see from the thirteenth tarot that
 the underbrush is fertilized with half-withered
           corpses and fleshless bones.
     “Why, where have you brought me, Fool?
              This is a cemetery!”
 And the Fool says, pointing to the invertebrate
          fauna feeding in the graves:
  “Here a monarchy reigns, mightier than you. .
His Majesty the Worm is a tabletop role-playing game       The game has robust procedures: characters adventure in
designed for dungeon-crawling. The Game Master             the Underworld, rest in camping scenes, then plan long-
uses the tools in this book to create a megadungeon        term actions in the City at the center of the Wide World.
called the Underworld. The players create adventurers
to explore the Underworld in pursuit of their personal     The relationships between companions, called Bonds,
quests. Tarot cards are used as a randomizing element.     power the rest and recovery mechanic of the game.
                                                           Role-playing drives the game forward.
This is a new-school game with old-school sensibilities.
It’s designed to make the “boring parts” interesting.      Combat encounters are handled with an action-packed
Slice-of-life subsystems like food, hunger, light,         subsystem that ensures that all players have interesting
and inventory management are central to play.              choices every minute of combat: no downtime!

                                                           We hope you will have fun with it!
Introduction
The Underworld blasphemes the earth under the City at the center of the world. Most
games begin with adventurers taking their first steps through the gate to the Underworld
from the City.

Game Principles
His Majesty the Worm aims to make dungeon exploration fun. It forefronts what might
otherwise be fringe rules for food, light, and time, and shines the spotlight on the visceral
experience of the dungeon crawl.

The (Demi-) Human Experience                                 Either way, the dragon provides some type of challenge
This game focuses on the personal experiences of the         for the adventurers, whether they are novices or veterans.
adventurers exploring the mythic Underworld.
                                                             Players should feel empowered to experiment and take
Players portray fantastic characters. However, the game      risks, with all the rewards and consequences that
is designed to make these adventurers feel real through      risk entails.
a persistent focus on basic “human” needs. Adventurers
will become cold, drunk, hungry, horny, stressed, happy,
hurt, etc. This allows players to immerse themselves in      The Deadly Underworld
the experience of their adventurer.                          The game—and the adventurer sheet—are actually pretty
                                                             simple. There are few numbers and not a lot of special
The essential meta-currency of the game are the Bonds        powers or abilities. There are no “spot checks”—only
the adventurers share with each other. When players          players describing where and how they’re searching.
role-play with their guild-mates, they charge these          There are no “disarm trap” skills—only players
Bonds. Players then spend these charges to recover from      describing how they move the knife across the tripwire
the mental and physical ailments accumulated from            or tap their ten-foot pole ahead of them.
dungeon delving.
                                                             Ultimately, this game is about exploring the
Rulings, Not Rules                                           Underworld. As such, there are no abilities that mitigate
                                                             the essential dangers of the dungeon.
Ultimately, no rule system completely encapsulates
every possibility of player action—and that’s the fun        • Darkness is always dangerous. No adventurer can see
of tabletop RPGs! There are fringe cases, strange              perfectly in the dark.
situations, and unconsidered possibilities that inevitably
arise during play. Having a GM to arbitrate these            • Rations and torches are always precious. There are no
situations is one of the advantages of tabletop games          “conjure food” spells, and the arts that sorcerers have
compared to other game forms. As such, these rules are         to conjure light are dangerous. Being bereft of light or
presented as a resource with the expectation that there        food means death.
will be ample homebrewing and hacking.
                                                             • Traps must always be navigated. There are no
When unexpected questions arise, GMs can adapt the             “perception” or “disarm” skills. Each trap is a unique
rules to fit the situation at hand. When that situation        puzzle to be solved.
comes up frequently, the GM and the table can
collaborate on turning that ruling into a more hard-and-     • Combat is always deadly. Healing is laborious,
fast rule. And, when hard-and-fast rules seem to fail the      requiring that the adventurers undertake a Camp
tests of common sense, verisimilitude, and fun, it’s the       Phase. Adventurers draw their swords at their
GM’s responsibility to make calls that change the rules        own peril.
for the better.
                                                             Whimsy
The Scaling Underworld                                       A fair bit of His Majesty the Worm is whimsy. This is an
The Underworld is not a place of balanced encounters.        RPG that knows it’s an RPG. You play adventurers who
There’s no expectation that the players are ever in a        know they are adventurers. It is playful with its tropes.
“level-appropriate” place. A sleeping dragon might be        It’s unpretentious. During a game, both players and
an unbeatable guardian for a beginning party and must        GMs will deconstruct and reconstruct common
be snuck past. A somewhat more experienced guild             dungeon delving tropes. This should be fun. This
might try and defeat the dragon to win her treasure.         should be delightful.

    The Four Phases
    Each adventurer has a personal quest (p. 24) that compels them into the lightless depths.
    Once their quest is fulfilled, they can finally retire and rest. Until then, it is a cycle of
    descending into the Underworld and returning to the City to restock and rest.

    The flow of the game consists of four distinct phases, each with its own style of play and rules.

    Against canon                              The Crawl Phase
    Throughout this book, there are            During the Crawl Phase, the guild explores an interconnected network of
    references to an implied setting           dungeons called the Underworld (p. 85). During this phase, adventurers test
    that are never elaborated on. We           their wits and skills against inhospitable forces in order to fulfill their quests.
    name and discuss people, places,           During the Crawl, players charge their Bonds with their guild-mates (p. 26).
    and historical events without              The Crawl is where you’ll spend most of your time.
    describing them in great detail. This
    is intentional.
                                               The Challenge Phase
    Instead of providing a gazetteer with      A Challenge Phase occurs when you need to focus on the beat-by-beat action
    everything carefully plotted out           (p. 107). This phase is when choices and consequences bear the hideous, overripe
    and a hundred-and-one nonsense             fruit of rotting bodies and terminated possibilities! During a Challenge, play
    fantasy words for you to memorize,         moves from a freeform style to a tactical system. Play is split up into rounds and
    we’ve painted with a fairly broad          turns, during which people perform various specific actions.
    brush. It’s our intention to give you
    a sense of scope and flavor without
    bogging the game down with lore to
    memorize or binding your story to a
    metaplot. The game world and the
    storyline are intended to vary from
                                                                “Many sink down and few
    table to table.                                              return to the sunlit lands.”
    It’s our hope that the implied
                                                                          – The Silver Chair, C.S. Lewis
    setting of His Majesty the Worm
    stimulates your imagination and
    allows you to tell the stories that
    you want to tell.

    As the setting details provided
    invoke a certain aesthetic for you,
                                               The Camp Phase
    we hope that you will use them.            As the adventurers get worn down by journeys and battles, they’ll pause and
    As the setting details provided feel       use the Camp Phase (p. 135). The focus of the Camp Phase is interpersonal role-
    frustrating in their obscurity or          playing, drama, and connections between members of the guild. During this
    contradictions, we hope you will           phase, players burn charged Bonds to rest and recover.
    change them, ignore them, or tear
    them physically from the book. At
    times, the provided material will be
                                               The City Phase
    inherently contradictory, obliging         Each delve is punctuated by the City Phase (p. 147). The City Phase resolves the

    The Flow of the Play
    Games usually take place at a regularly scheduled time and place. Finding time to play
    games with other busy people can be challenging. Consistent play is crucial to keeping a
    game alive. Most sessions have a basic flow:


    Before play                                                 During play
    At the start of a game session, a few important pieces of   A typical game session flows between the different
    bookkeeping are taken care of:                              phases. Over the course of many game sessions, play will
                                                                follow this sequence:
    Recap                                                       • Decide to pursue one adventurer’s quest.
    One player—with help from others at the table, and
    with corrections from the GM as needed—recaps what          • Adventure through the Underworld (Crawl Phase).
    happened during the last session. This gets everybody
    back into the game and refreshes their memory about         • Struggle against the strange denizens of the
    where they were and what they’re doing.                       Underworld (Challenge Phase).

    If this player does an exceptionally good job, the GM       • Rest as well as possible in the lightless depths
    may give them a point of Resolve (p. 32). They may keep       (Camp Phase).
    this Resolve or give it to another player who needs it.
                                                                • Return to the City, broken and bleeding (City Phase).
    Returning players                                             • Spend accumulated wealth to heal, stock up on
    If anyone misses a session during the Crawl Phase,              equipment, and pursue long-term projects in the City.
    their adventurer is assumed to be about one room away,
    trailing behind the main guild. They have been slowed         • Pick up a contract to finance the next crawl (p. 46).
    down performing a Camp Action (p. 137). When the
    player returns, they tell the table what activity they      • Descend back into the Underworld in continued
    performed, receive the benefit from it, and rejoin the        pursuit of the current quest while working on their
    main group. Some actions (e.g., Fellowship, Train)            contract (Crawl Phase).
    logically require another adventurer to be “absent” with
    the returning player; only choose activities that make      • Repeat.
    sense for the circumstances.

    It is the science of imaginary solutions                    time. It’s best for the GM to close play when there’s a

4        CHAPTER 1       |     THE BASICS
Adjudicating the game: GM responses
An RPG is a conversation between the GM and the players. The GM describes a scene
and the players describe their actions inside the scene. The GM and the players ask
questions of each other to further define their shared textual reality.


The GM adjudicates how the adventurers’ actions               Even difficult tasks can be resolved without a test of fate
impact the world. To this end, GMs are armed with the         as long as:
following four stock phrases:                                 1. there’s no interesting risk;
                                                              2. the adventurer has plenty of time;
• “Yes, you can do that.”                                     3. they have the appropriate tools.

• “Say more about what you’re doing.”                         If one of these factors is missing, it’s time to move to one
                                                              of the other responses.
• “Draw to see if you can do that.”
                                                              If an adventurer's actions would incur some sort of
• “No, you can’t do that.”                                    penalty, the GM should make that clear and give them
                                                              a choice.
These phrases (and their variants) are the four basic
responses that a GM has for answering a player when           • If an adventurer’s actions would take a long time
they ask, “Can my character do…?”                               to complete, the GM should make this clear. If the
                                                                player elects to spend the time, the GM draws on the
                                                                Meatgrinder table (p. 91) to represent time passing;
“Yes, you can do that”                                          similar to the “Moving carefully” rules on page 91.
                                                                Draw from the major arcana—torches gutter on a
The player describes their adventurer’s actions and the         result of I-V.
GM simply describes what happens. If there’s nothing
preventing the adventurer from succeeding, they               • If an adventurer's actions would create a lot of noise,
simply succeed.                                                 the GM should give that info. If the player elects to
                                                                risk the noise, the GM draws on the Meatgrinder
• “It doesn’t seem that the door is locked. You open the        table to represent an interested predator investigating
  door slowly and carefully.”                                   the disturbance; similar to the “Loud noises” rules
                                                                on page 91. The GM draws from the major arcana—a
• “Sure, you can climb the tree. There're plenty                random encounter occurs on a result of XV-XX.
  of handholds.”

• “You know that it will take a few minutes of hard work      “Say more about what you’re doing”
  and it'll make a shit ton of noise, but of course you can   Sometimes it’s not exactly clear what actions the players
  use your felling axe to hack down the wooden door.”         are describing or what their intentions are. In these cases,
                                                              the GM should ask for clarification.
Players portray members of the unfortunate caste called
“adventurers.” As such, they have the skills and abilities    • “How exactly are you searching for traps?”
that you’d assume adventurers would have by default.
                                                              • “OK, because of the Linguist talent, you definitely
In practice, this means you ignore all the uninteresting        speak the myconid language, but you know that
parts of adventuring. You never test fate to see if an          their language is expressed entirely in the medium of

    Once the GM has achieved clarity with “Say more,” they

    “Draw to see if you can do that”                                   The Challenge Phase
    When an action is fraught with danger or its outcome is            It’s worth noting that the rules of the Challenge
    uncertain, it’s time to test fate. For an overview of tests        Phase are more bounded than the freeform
    of fate, see page 8.                                               nature of standard play. The Challenge Actions
                                                                       and the player’s hand of cards usually determine
    Tests of fate should be relatively rare and relatively tense.      what an adventurer can and can’t do. The GM
    Don’t call for tests of fate for inconsequential actions—          still adjudicates what the players try to do when
    only when something of importance hangs in the balance.            there’s ambiguity:

    • “The door is locked. If you have lockpicks, you can              “Oh, you’re trying to squeeze past the slime as they

     Tests of Fate
     When an adventurer’s action within the game's narrative is uncertain, the GM calls for a
     test of fate.
     Adventurers have four attributes, rated 1-4. Each                There are four possible outcomes to a test of fate.
     represents an “approach” towards problem solving, and
     says a lot about how an adventurer achieves their goal.

     The GM determines which attribute is most relevant               If the total value is 14+, the result is a success. The

     attribute is being tested.

The Fool has a value of 0.

• If you pull the Fool initially during a test of fate, you
  can push fate as normal. This could turn the test from a
  failure to a success or to a great failure.

• If you pull the Fool when pushing fate, your result
  automatically becomes a great failure.

When the Fool is drawn, remember to shuffle both the
minor and major arcana decks.

     When negative factors would hinder an adventurer, they         consequences of the test. If the test of fate is successful,

Bound by fate
Whether you succeed or fail, your results are bound         The GM totals the amount of hits to determine the
by fate. You cannot retry the same test unless the          success of the group test.
circumstances significantly change. If you fail to pick a
lock, that lock is beyond your adventurer’s abilities. If   • 2 hits: Success for the entire group.
you fail to climb a wall, that wall is unclimbable.
                                                            • 1 hit: The group comes short of succeeding and are put
But maybe the warrior in the company can bash down            in a tight spot.
the door. And maybe the sorcerer has a magical cloak
that allows you to fly over the wall. You’ll have to find   • 0 hits: Failure for the entire group.
another way past an obstacle if you fail in the test.
                                                            • <0 hits: Disaster for the entire group.
You can also attempt a test again if the circumstances
significantly change. Significant change usually means      Like other tests of fate, group tests are bound by fate.
new ideas, new tools, or a new twist on an old situation.

Because His Majesty the Worm is a fundamentally
collaborative game, fellow guild members are also bound     Example group test

     Effects
     Terms that describe consequences that happen to characters or objects—things like Blind,
     Destroy, and Heal—are called Effects. Each effect has its own rules and implications,
     explained in the list below.

     Blind                                                         Exhaust
     Blinded creatures cannot see or gain any visual               Exhausted creatures make all tests and Challenge
     information.                                                  Actions with disfavor.

       with disfavor.

     • All harmful actions against Blind creatures have favor.     Healed creatures instantly remove one Wound from

     completed, the effect ends.                                   seven Dispositions to the best of their ability, following

       perform the commanded action. The total value for           are: anger, distaste, sadness, joy, surprise, trust, fear.
       the Controlled action is equal to the value of the action
       used to Control it.
                                                                   Grow/Shrink
     Curse                                                         Grown creatures and objects double their original height.
                                                                   Shrunk creatures and objects half their original height.

     by the GM. Turned to stone by a medusa? Fused with            Gain favor when this would be advantageous (squeezing

Trip
Tripped creatures fall prone.
• Prone creatures cannot Avoid, Move, or Dash.
• Melee attacks against prone targets have favor.
• Missile attacks against prone targets have disfavor.
• Anybody engaged with a Tripped creature immediately disengages (p. 109).




    Effect names
    Note that capitalized effect names
    change conjugation depending on
    how they’re used in game text but all
    mean the same thing. For example,
    a Blinding attack Blinds a creature,
    after which they are Blinded.

                                                                           CHAPTER 2     |   THE ADVENTURER                15
     The Player’s Manifesto
     An RPG is simply an exchange of questions and answers between the players and the GM.
     These questions and answers can have nuance and texture. When playing His Majesty the
     Worm, this manifesto will help you frame your conversations with your GM.


     Be careful, be fierce                                     Solve problems orthogonally
     You don’t start out a hero. The only thing between        You should be trying to make your GM say: “I didn’t
     you and a salivating dragon’s jaws are a few conditions   even think of that.”
     unchecked on your adventurer sheet. You should never
     expect the world around you to be fair. You’re not in     In an RPG, you can do anything. That’s the appeal!
     a tutorial level; your adventurer is journeying through   When you’re playing a computer game, you can only
     a mythic Underworld that wants them to stay forever       do the things the game designer programmed in. They
     and ever. Keeping them alive requires caution and         anticipated you moving left, right, and down. Going up
     thoughtfulness.                                           is out of the question. Not so in a tabletop game.

     Encountering a dragon is different when your adventurer   Most problems aren’t solved by fighting them. People
     is inexperienced versus when they’re experienced. At      can be reasoned with. Monsters can be placated. Traps
     first, the focus might be stealth—how much gold can       can be avoided. Monsters can be led into traps. People
     you get away with before the dragon notices you? After    can be sold the monster’s guts.
     you’ve built up your strength, you might feel confident
     enough to engage in combat with the dragon. But don’t     Don’t expect to “use” your talents and motifs to solve a
     fight fair. Make sure you choose the battleground.        problem. The abilities and items you have listed are just
     Ambush the dragon. Drop a rock on its head.               tools—and they’re only one of the many tools in your
                                                               arsenal. Think outside of your adventurer sheet.
     And when the going gets tough, don’t be afraid to cut
     your losses and run away.
                                                               Engage the world
                                                               You don’t have to talk in a silly voice or wear a costume*.
                                                               You do, however, have to interact with the fiction of the
                                                               world in a logical way.

                                                               The essential way you have to interact with the fictional
                                                               world is to ask questions. By engaging your GM in a
                                                               give-and-take, you make the game real. The game world
                                                               is layered. By asking questions, you begin to understand
                                                               its bounds.

                                                               There are no abilities on your adventurer sheet that
                                                               give you the sort of insight that asking questions will
                                                               provide. If you’re looking for a trap, pour water on the
                                                               ground and see if you can find any trap doors. If you’re
                                                               looking for a secret door, tap on the walls and listen for
                                                               something hollow.

                                                               The game is about you using your real-life thinking
                                                               brain to solve problems, overcome obstacles, and figure
                                                               things out. There are no stats or powers that are going to
                                                               help you solve the essential issues.

                                                               * You can though. We won’t stop you.

  step back. Share each other's burdens. Revel in each           – Introduction to the I Ching, Carl Jung
  other's successes.

• Be respectful and considerate. If you want to explore
  a particular story, engage with your fellow players
  to make sure they're comfortable with the themes
  that you're exploring. Don't be “that guy.” Read the
  goddamn room.

• Let your relationships grow and change. Every session
  or two, touch base with another player. Discuss how
  your adventurers feel about each other in light of your
  most recent experiences. Have rivals become allies?
  Have allies become best friends? Have best friends
  become lovers?

• Be funny in character. Be serious in character. Think in
  character. Stay in character.



Embrace the chaos
Part of the game is skill. Part of the game is chance.
Sometimes, you can’t be careful or fierce enough to
avoid a test of fate. And when fate isn’t on your side,
you have to embrace it. Having something bad happen
doesn’t mean that you’ve made a mistake. It’s just part of
the game.

It is easy to create a new adventurer. This is on purpose.
If your adventurer dies, throw yourself into the next one.
If your adventurer completes their quest, be excited to
retire them.

Games without consequences have no teeth. How boring
would it be if you knew you would never fail and never
die? The essential gimmick of question/answer with
the GM would be boring: “How will your adventurer
succeed today?” Thus, love the chaos.




                                                                 CHAPTER 2        |   THE ADVENTURER        17
     Session 0
     Sometimes, RPG players are expected to create their characters by themselves and
     show up on game night expecting to meet everyone else at an inn. This can sometimes
     lead to problems at the game table. We recommend that the players and the GM get
     together for a session before play starts to create adventurers and talk about everybody's
     expectations. This is called “session 0,” and it can go a long way towards making sure
     everybody is having fun.

     The Call to Adventure
     Creating an adventurer means heeding the call to adventure. When you create an
     adventurer, you answer questions and make a series of decisions. This will result in a
     character with a background, a history, equipment, and connections to other adventurers.

     Track the choices of the Call to Adventure and subsequent play on your adventurer sheet.
     A full version of the adventurer sheet can be printed at hismajestytheworm.games.

                                                                            CHAPTER 2   |   THE ADVENTURER                      27
 6 Arête
Each adventurer has the capacity to exemplify the
platonic ideal of their kin, which is called their arête.

Arête (AIR-uh-tay) is a word of Greek origin meaning
virtue, gnosis, excellence, and evolution.

Each kin has an arête talent. Unlike talents associated
with an adventurer’s path, arête talents cannot be trained
with experience points.

You gain arête when you perform certain accomplishments
dependent on your kith. The first time you accomplish
each particular deed, put a check mark beside it. When
you have checked off all three of your arête triggers, you
gain your arête talent. See chapter 4 for a list of your
kith’s arête triggers and arête talent.
 7       Languages                                            Tylwyth
There are five languages spoken commonly in the City,         Tylwyth is the ancestral language of the fay and other
and a hundred uncommon ones. At a minimum, each               spirits. Since the fay have dwelt within the bounds of the
adventurer is at least bilingual—choose two languages         Wide World for much longer than Mankind, many of the
from the lists below. If you want to learn more               spirits and minor divinities that live there speak Tylwyth
languages later, train the Loremaster talent until you’re     almost exclusively.
a skilled linguist.
                                                              The fay, as a whole, are known for their love of
Alternatively, if tracking languages in your game doesn’t     languages and Tylwyth enjoys a certain fame among
feel fun, don’t do it.                                        scholars and linguists as being a logical, subtle, and
                                                              beautiful tongue. Careful cultivation by immortal
Vulgaris                                                      linguists has developed Tylwyth into a purposeful and

         Hirelings?
         There are no rules for hirelings, henchmen,
         mercenaries, etc. because that is what you are
         playing. If you’re going into the Underworld,
         you’re an adventurer. You’re going down there for
         some reason, not just gold. Nobody can go into
         the Underworld unless they’re a member of a
         guild and nobody is special enough to join a guild
         unless they’re going to be played by a player.

Use your adventurer sheet to track where you’re carrying your items. You have             craftsmanship or go on a truly
four slots to carry items on your belt, twenty-one slots in your pack, and (of            epic bender.

During Challenges, it’s easier to get things off of your belt (see “Pull Item
from Belt,” p. 120) than out of your pack (see “Pull Item from Pack,” p. 118).

One of the things you track in your supply resources is your light source—see
pages 94‑95 for rules on light and flickers. Note which hand you’re carrying it in.

The adventurer sheet also contains circles so that you can track your gear’s
durability. When an item’s durability is compromised, it suffers a Notch.

• Fragile items break after 1 Notch.
• Items intended for durability break after 2.
• Items made of tempered steel can suffer 3.
Notched items can be repaired with a tinker's kit or in the City.

A list of adventuring items is provided on page 164.




                                                                            CHAPTER 2   |   THE ADVENTURER                     37
                                      Retirement
                                      Your quest is the reason you are adventuring. The
                                      Underworld sucks. Normal, healthy-brained people
                                      don’t want to go there. When you complete your quest,
                                      there are two options: retire your adventurer or declare a
                                      new quest.

                                      When you retire an adventurer, your next adventurer
                                      gains one of the following for each 10XP your retired
                                      adventurer had:

                                      • 1 mastered talent from any path
                                      • 1 arête check mark
                                      Retired adventurers live in the City and are under the
                                      command of the GM.

                                      Alternatively, it is possible to declare a new quest
                                      to avoid retiring your adventurer. Perhaps, while
                                      adventuring, you have found a new reason to journey to
                                      the Underworld.

                                      If you declare a new quest, you gain 3XP for completing
                                      your last quest like everybody else in the guild. Your new
                                      quest should make sense in context and be related to the
                                      adventures you’ve had. However, you always have to have
                                      some reason to go back down into the Underworld. That
                                      place seriously sucks.

                                      Note that adventurers who die and are lost in the
                                      Underworld do not transfer any XP to a new character
                                      without use of the Hold a Funeral City Action (p. 158).




                                      New adventurer
                                      checklist
                                      If you have retired your previous adventurer, or if you
                                      are a new player just joining the game, the checklist on
                                      the following page will help you integrate your new
                                      adventurer without the processes of a group-focused
                                      Call to Adventure or session 0.




38   CHAPTER 2   |   THE ADVENTURER
     NEW ADVENTURER CHECKLIST
If you’re a new player joining a group playing His Majesty the Worm and you
missed session 0, here are the things you need to prepare.



Prior to your first session
• Have your adventurer sheet ready.
• Have your kin talent and all seven path talents written down.
• Determine which path talent you have mastered. The rest are in training.
• Choose items from the Omphalic Market (p. 162) – 1 luxurious item, 5 common items, and as many
  impoverished items as you want. Items needed for one of your talents are impoverished items for you.

• Know your own name.


At your first session
• At the beginning of the session, select two players with whom you have Bonds.
• Say what your adventurer looks like.
• Ask questions. Ask about the game world. Ask about the rules. Ask for help about which actions to take.
  Ask for clarification about how things work.

• Give feedback. Let the GM know how it went. Let them know if there’s something you thought could
  have gone better. Let them know if there was something you liked.



Prior to your second session
• Based on your experiences in your first session, fill out a Bond for every member of the Guild.


At the end of your second session
• Based on your experiences in your second session, either join the current guild or elect to create a new
  adventurer that’s more appealing to you or who meshes with the group dynamic better.

• If you join the guild, sign the guild roster and state your role and marching order.
• If you join the guild, you’ll join their current quest and gain 3 XP.

     Collectively, you and your other adventurers form a guild during the Call to Adventure.
     In the same way that you track your adventurer by way of your adventurer sheet, the
     entire table tracks the guild by way of the guild roster (printed on the following pages).
     The guild roster can be downloaded from hismajestytheworm.games.

      2 Terms
     The guild roster defines your guild’s rules for looting
     rights. The default contract stipulates that all members
     of the guild split loot equally and funeral rights are paid
     for by the guild.

     As you fill out the guild roster, take a moment to talk
     about your guild’s looting rights, who gets the most
     shares, how expenses are arranged, what happens to
     fallen adventurers’ gear, etc.

                                                                 Deeds and Fame
     The Underworld has monsters and it has treasure.
     Powerful, influential, and rich people want things in
     the Underworld. They offer contracts: risk for reward.
     Do what they want in the Underworld and they’ll make        When great deeds are done in the Underworld, the

                                                                             CHAPTER 4      |   KITH AND KIN        49
     Humans
     When does pride become hubris? When does glory tarnish to vainglory? This thin line is
     embodied in humans, the knaves and the kings of the Wide World.

     Humans are not as hardy as the immortal fay, being          Even so, they are fractious. Humanity has never
     given to sickness and age. Nor are they as crafty as the    united themselves under a single banner (though
     underfolk, being slow to develop the crafts of alchemy      various warlords have attempted the feat). Matters of
     and lore of natural philosophy. Yet humanity has one        philosophy, religion, or blood will divide them—as
     gift that surpasses every other: war.                       will ambition. Therefore, the power of men is spread
                                                                 through a handful of notable empires and hundreds of
     Humankind is built for war. The crafts they have learned    petty kingdoms.
     from dwarves and elves have been turned ingeniously to
     this purpose. They breed and mature quickly to resupply     Still, humans display many praiseworthy traits. They are
     their cities with men and women, replacing those lost to    loyal folk, lauding fidelity as the most noble of virtues.
                    hardship. They are fierce, doughty, and      They long remember the deeds of their fathers in song
                       brave. Using their arts of war, mankind   and story, and strive to emulate them. This, in turn,
                        has conquered much of the Wide           creates a drive to win glory and renown for their families.
                        World. They are the conquering kings,    Their communities are strengthened by this desire for
                                      proud and terrible.        fame, as they eschew the unworthy for fear of
                                                                 bringing shame to their lineage. Indeed, few folk are
                                                                 more fiercely protective of their kith and kin than
                                                                 mankind. They have a great capacity for kindness, for
                                                                 all their ferocity.

                                                                                           When elves realized that they
                                                                                          could not generate new life (only
                                                                                   reincarnate), they decided to solve
                                                                                      the problem like they solved many

                                                                                        the children of mortal mothers,
                                                                                         rationalizing that they would
                                                                                          “save” the children from eventual
                                                                                          old age and death. They used
                                                                                         rites from the realm of dreams,
                                                                                      transforming the children from
                                                                                    mortal to immortal.

                                                                                   change the infants into elven children.
                                                                                   They were mistaken. It transformed

                                                                                   youthful, they became eternally bent
                                                                                   and aged.

                                                                              CHAPTER 4        |   KITH AND KIN             57
     Underfolk
     Beneath your feet there are worlds. There are lives lived, tragedies experienced, arguments
     made, trysts discovered. There are wars fought, there are treasures wrought. Beneath
     your feet, there are the underfolk.


     The term “underfolk” refers to three distinct kins—the     The underfolk are the progenitors of civilization. True,
     dwarves, the halflings, and the trolls. The underfolk,     humans really ran with the concept, but dwarves first
     however, consider themselves to be one people. Dwarves     thought of it. Writing systems, advanced math, complex
     and halflings consider themselves to be the same race,     forms of government, written contracts, common
     and happily consider trolls to be adopted siblings.        law—all underfolk inventions. These were all taught to
     Humans have trouble getting along, finding ways to split   humanity when humans first came to the Wide World
     hairs over religion and heredity. The underfolk have no    from parts unknown. The underfolk and humans have
     such difficulties—they consider themselves one family.     always been allies.

                                                                Underfolk society is ruled by the Council of Liveries.
                                                                This is not as much of a plutocracy as it seems at first.

                                                                Everybody in underfolk society is liveried—that is, a
                                                                member of a mercantile organization—so everybody
                                                                ostensibly has a voice. That’s the theory anyway.

                                                                The underfolk have a practical view of religion. They
                                                                acknowledge that the various deities of the men and
                                                                elves might be real and potent, but also rationalize that
                                                                these deities probably don’t care about the poor little
                                                                underfolk hiding from their gaze under the earth. They
                                                                do not believe that their spirits, on death, depart to any
                                                                afterlife. Their souls are too heavy. They believe they all
                                                                linger in the plane of Flesh after death as ghosts. Ghosts,
                                                                of course, have needs too. That’s why the underfolk
                                                                construct large tombs full of nice things to occupy
                                                                themselves when they finally die.

                                                                Since cities tend to get filled with tombs, underfolk are
                                                                always tunneling out new homes. Whole cities have been
                                                                left behind that are just necropoli now.

                                                                                  CHAPTER 4        |   KITH AND KIN               61
     Orcs
     A prayer to Rng: “O’ Rng, gracious and kind. We have all that we need. Your
     people are content and happy. Our lives are full, and we need nothing else.
     Please, visit your gifts on our enemies. Give them what they lack. Let them know
     your love and generosity.”

     At home, orcs are much like everybody else. They have       It's said that orcs have a fire in their guts that is only
     families. They have farms. They like to drink horns         quenched by the presence of gold. Without gold, orcs
     of mead with their friends. They make crafts to sell at     really are crazy. Why do they take royalty? Well,
     their religious festivals. They worry about their sick      nobody knows. Sometimes they ransom them to their
     goats. Few people see this side of the orcs, though. Most   noble houses for larger sums of gold. Sometimes they
     people only see the raiders.                                don't, though.

     Orcs are famous raiders and traders. They travel all over   Slavery is against the Orc-Law (an oral collection of
     the Wide World and are the most accomplished seafarers.     laws and traditions), so royals that become permanent
     In the summer months, when the icy straits melt between     residents of orcish lands are usually integrated.
     their lands and the kingdoms of men, parties of orc         Sometimes they spend the rest of their lives in the frozen
     raiders come plundering. They take gold and royalty.        north. Sometimes they're rescued by crusaders. About a
                                                                 hundred years ago, three major campaigns (and several
                                                                 minor ones) were mounted by various noble houses to
                                                                 win back some of these captives from the orcs. These
                                                                 campaigns are very much in the mind of both humans
                                                                 and orcs in the modern era.

                                                                 Orcs are mostly matrilineal. This is because some orcs
                                                                 don't have fathers. Orcs can reproduce asexually through
                                                                 parthenogenesis. This type of reproduction (curiously
                                                                 enough) produces both male and female orcs; each orc is
                                                                 a half-clone of their mother.

                                                                 A baby orc is called a goblin. Unlike human children,
                                                                 who take years to learn to walk and talk, goblins learn
                                                                 these skills incredibly quickly. Within a few days, a baby
                                                                 goblin is up on its feet, walking and talking and fighting
                                                                 and picking locks. Really, the little guys are remarkable.

                                                                 Not that they're cruel, but orcs have a somewhat blasé
                                                                 concern for their offspring's health. Few goblins get to
                                                                 grow up to be orcs. It's a rough world. It's better for
                                                                 an orc parent to survive long enough to make another
                                                                 clutch of goblin babies than it is for a single goblin (or
                                                                 even an entire clutch) to survive. Prioritize the elders.

                                                                             CHAPTER 5     |   THE FOUR PATHS               67
             Path of Swords
The initial forays into the Underworld were grisly affairs. It was plaster miners who
discovered the passage into the first level. They curiously chiseled their way into the
antechambers. Like tomb robbers, they discovered gilded treasures and heaps of ancient
coins piled therein. And then they discovered the grue. There were no survivors.

Before the First Crusade was finally mobilized, the death toll rose terribly as the lure
of the Underworld proved irresistible to the very brave and the very foolish. As more of
the Underworld began to be revealed, more creatures slithered out of half-remembered
legends into reality. Strange beasts and malevolent entities crawled up out of the opened
chambers and into the terrorized City. The Cult, at first overwhelmed with the practical
considerations and theological questions the Underworld posed, united the proud and
ancient houses of mankind with fiery speeches. Under the Cult’s leadership, the First
Crusade hunted the monsters that had escaped into the City and encamped themselves on
the threshold of the Underworld, warding the lands of men from further attacks.

It was only during the Second Crusade that it was discovered that those who die in the
Underworld do not stay dead...

Common motifs:
would-be knight, deposed king, charming pirate, retired gladiator, fanatic vampire hunter, barbarian warrior poet

                                                                           CHAPTER 5     |    THE FOUR PATHS                 71
               Path of Pentacles
Treasure was, and remains, a powerful motivator for Underworld expeditions. The spires
of the Castle of Crossed Destinies were literally covered in gold plating until explorers
stripped them and hauled the plates back to the surface. The Underworld denizens
possess strange coinage as well: round pieces of gold stamped with the faces of three
beautiful women and a pentacle star on the reverse. Who these ancient sovereigns were is a
matter of great scholarly debate and fanciful public speculation.

By the same token, treasure is the primary motivator for the City’s current system of
adventuring guilds. The fifty percent guild tax on recovered loot is a heavy burden for
adventurers and is much bemoaned. The tax collectors posted at each known exit from the
Underworld are a particularly hated lot, but the City has grown rich from this system.
Of course, these heavy taxes have created a sprawling industry of smuggling, bribery,
and fencing. In pursuit of both relic hunting and black marketeering, “thief” has become a
particularly common profession.

Common motifs:
arrogant duelist, feral scavenger, morbid jester, bounty hunter, traitorous spy, urchin pickpocket, penitent assassin

74        CHAPTER 5        |   THE FOUR PATHS
             Path of Cups
When the Underworld opened, so many went on the quest for the Grail of Mythrys
that a massive support system, both secular and religious, was assembled. Inns and
public houses for the housing of pilgrims, coin changers for foreigners, shops of supply
and purveyance, smithies for armament, chapels and shrines for the devout, charlatans
and peddlers selling false maps and rumors, scribes and lawyers for drafting of charters
and wills, apothecaries for the healing of those returned unsuccessful—all these sprang up
almost overnight. The sign of the Cup has become synonymous for these tradesmen, as
well as having a holy connotation, and is still used today to advertise needful service.

Common motifs:
grisly apothecary, adventurous cartographer, jolly cleric, daring archaeologist, jaded barber surgeon, young insect tamer

                                                                        CHAPTER 5       |   THE FOUR PATHS               79
             Path of Wands
The relationship between the City and magic has been long fraught with bloodshed
and sorrow. During the Age of the First Empire, sorcery was used as an act of worship
towards the Crow-Headed Queen——one of the earliest deified empresses. During the Age of
the Republic, sorcery was seen as being fundamentally tied to both monarchists and elves,
and it was made illegal. Still, several cabals flourished in secret. The Age of the Republic
was marked by the increasing fanaticism of witch hunters as they attempted to root out
these hidden sorcerers.

A blanket ban on sorcery proved impossible with the advent of the Age of Dungeon. Too
many trials and foes in the Underworld were essentially mystical in nature. The practice
of sorcery became a necessary evil, and the Cult began to draw up the appropriate pardons
and indulgences.

Today, those who practice sorcery in the City must be licensed and registered with the
crown. Official sorcerers are granted rods of office by the Tower Gnostic and allowed
to join guilds in the exploration of the Underworld. Unofficial sorcery is punishable by
fines, but is largely unregulated as long as it is not performed in the City itself. Still, the
Witch Finder General remains an influential figure within City politics, and his templars
have a much grimmer view of unregulated sorcery.

Common motifs:
court mage, insane astrologer, artisanal wand maker, conniving charlatan, morbid wizard, doomsday cultist

                                                                       CHAPTER 6        |   THE CRAWL PHASE              85
     The Flow of the Crawl Phase
     A new game of His Majesty the Worm starts at the gates to the Underworld.
     The Crawl begins with the guild taking their first steps into those lightless depths.


                                               The Crawl is the phase of the game centered on exploring the Underworld.
     The mythic underworld                     When the guild leaves the safety of civilization to pursue their quests,
     His Majesty the Worm’s setting is a       negotiating with strange creatures, avoiding traps, and excavating ancient
     place described in fiction, folklore,     treasures, they are Crawling. Most of the game is focused on this phase.
     and games as a mythic underworld.
     A mythic underworld is not merely         The Underworld is what is called a megadungeon. A megadungeon is
     a cave system with kobolds and            inherently strange. It does not need to conform to the players’ conceptions and
     goblins hiding in every shadowy           expectations. It does benefit from having internal logic, however. Learning the
     corner. It is another world,              “rules” of the Underworld is fun, and having internally consistent logic allows
     charged with unconventional               players to make meaningful choices (which is the point of the game).
     physics, inhuman entities, and
     alien architectures.                      A megadungeon is composed of smaller, constituent dungeons. Each dungeon
                                               is a thematic level, section, or subsection. For example, your Underworld
                                               might be composed of five dungeon levels, which are called the Spires, the
     Characteristics of a                      Castle of Crossed Destinies, the Inverted Castle, the City of Ruin, and the
     mythic underworld                         Necropolis of Ot.
     1. It’s big, and has many levels; in
     fact, it may be endless                   Dungeons are separated into different rooms. A room can be any discrete
     2. It follows its own ecological and      space: a chamber, a feasting hall, a natural cavern, an underground river, etc.
     physical rules                            Each room should have something interesting for the players to interact with.
     3. It is not static; the inhabitants      For example, one room in the Castle of Crossed Destinies could have a giant
     and even the layout may grow or           throne constructed of a titan’s bones, another room could be the lair of a
     change over time                          reverse sphinx who needs to hear riddles to survive, and so on.
     4. It is not linear
     5. There are many ways to move up         As the guild explores each room, random events called the Meatgrinder create
     and down through the levels               tension. The Meatgrinder represents the passage of time: torches burning low,
     6. Its purpose is mysterious or           patrolling monsters, and other hazards.
     shrouded in legend
     7. It’s inimical to those exploring it    Each dungeon level has both a map and a Meatgrinder table, both full of
     8. Deeper or farther levels are more      interesting things to discover. When players travel into a new room, the GM
     dangerous                                 looks at the room description. Simultaneously, the GM draws a random card
     9. It’s a (the?) central feature of the   from the major arcana and consults the Meatgrinder table. They then describe
     campaign                                  the newly-entered room in the context of the random Meatgrinder encounter.

 “Folk like to pretend they know everything about the world. [. .]                   cross the invisible bridge.


 You don’t have blanks on your map, so the folks who draw them
  shade in a piece and write, ‘The Eld.’ You might as well burn a
      hole right through the map for what good that does.”
                    – The Wise Man’s Fear, Patrick Rothfuss




Despite the presence of otherworldly and strange beings, very few creatures
attack on sight and fight to the death. (Well, perhaps skeletons. They want to
free their boney brethren from the flesh prisons that you’re cruelly keeping
them in.) Almost everything can be talked to, negotiated with, or at least
avoided. See “Disposition” on page 99 for an overview of negotiating with the
GM’s characters.

When combat cannot be avoided, the Crawl Phase transitions into the
Challenge Phase. Once the Challenge is resolved, the Challenge Phase
transitions back to the Crawl.

Mysteriously, the Underworld has a property that preserves life. When a
mortal blow is dealt, the victim lingers at Death’s Door before dying. This
property has prolonged the life of many adventurers who have run afoul of
the Underworld’s treachery.

Those who do die in the Underworld rise again as undead…




                                                                         CHAPTER 6   |   THE CRAWL PHASE                    87
     Abandon All Hope, Ye Who Enter Here
     As you explore, you will find hazards that need to be navigated around, avoided, or
     retreated from.

     This is a game about interacting with the world as if it
     actually exists. Because RPGs are conversation games,          Secret doors
     you explore the game world through asking questions.           Some doors are secret. These doors might be obscured
     You can ask what your adventurer can see, feel, hear, etc.     (behind a bookshelf ) or built to be all but invisible (stone
     No need to draw cards—just ask what you can perceive           doors that only open when you twist a candle sconce).
     and the GM will answer you honestly. As the GM
     describes things, follow up with specific questions to dig     You find secret doors by describing how you search for
     deeper into the game world.                                    them. You can look at a wall to see if you can see any
                                                                    seams. You can tap on a wall to hear if it sounds hollow.
     There’s no list of skills or abilities to limit what you can   You can look behind curtains, inside wardrobes, and
     do within the fictional world. Don’t ask “Can I make           under rugs to see if there’s anything there.
     some sort of test to look for…” or “Can I make a test to

     Example Meatgrinder table
     Card Meatgrinder Event
       I.     Torches gutter

       II.    Torches gutter

      III.    Torches gutter

       IV.    Torches gutter

       V.     Torches gutter

              [Curiosity] Local Fauna: The guild startles up a flock of luminescent cave butterflies. They flutter
      VI.
              away quickly.

      VII.    [Curiosity] Cockatrice Call: The guild hears a cockatrice’s peacock-like shriek, distantly.

              [Curiosity] Orcish Graffiti: The guild notices some graffiti in Vetus chalked onto the cavern wall. It
      VIII.   reads: “Ulf is no true orc. If he wishes to win my hand in marriage, he must defeat me in combat.” (The
              GM can accept lore bids on this curiosity as appropriate.)

              [Curiosity] Blind Fish Pool: The guild wanders by a shallow pool. The water looks clear, but the pool
      IX.
              is full of toothy, blind fish.

              [Curiosity] Nearby Flowers: The air is full of a heady floral scent. If the guild searches around a little,
              they’ll find a bunch of pale blue and purple lilies sprouting nearby. Appropriate lore bids will show that
       X.
              they are normal flowers with few (if any) meaningful alchemical properties, but they are quite lovely and
              might make a nice bouquet for someone.

              [Travel event] Droppings: The first person in the marching order accidentally steps in some droppings. If
      XI.     they can’t find a way to get clean soon, they’ll become Stressed. If the guild investigates, they realize that
              the droppings are from an ogre. It looks no more than a day old.

              [Travel event] Rushing River: The guild encounters a rushing river which has risen past its banks. It’s
              impossible to ford without getting soaked. The guild can either turn back and try and find an alternate
              route or attempt to cross. Swimming across the river requires a test of Swords. If successful, they make
      XII.
              it across safely. If the test fails, they suffer a Wound from almost drowning. Whether successful or not,
              anybody who braved the cold waters becomes Stressed. If no precautions were taken, fragile items in
              backpacks (scrolls, provisions) are soaked and Destroyed.




92     CHAPTER 6       |   THE CRAWL PHASE
Card Meatgrinder Event
         [Travel event] Hole in Pack: While traveling, a random adventurer discovers that their pack has a hole
XIII.    in it. The last listed item in their pack has fallen out and disappeared. (Backtracking and performing a
         thorough search will prompt additional watches to pass.)

         [Travel event] Bad Scene: The guild comes upon a field of faintly glowing green mushrooms
         sporadically sending up little clouds of dust. In the middle of the field is a corpse in rusted armor. A
XIV.
         cracked chest lies near the corpse. (It’s all bad news. Mushrooms are poisonous. Corpse is a zombie.
         Chest? Probably bad too. But there’s also gold in the chest and that’s good.)

         [Travel event] Webs: The guild’s path forward is blocked by thick layers of web. However, they can
 XV.     see several hanging sacks dangling from the cavern ceiling. Are these other adventurers who met a grim
         fate? Could they be rescued?

         [Random encounter] Red Herring Tavern: The guild happens upon a squat but cozy-looking tavern.
         A wooden sign depicts a red fish leaping from the water (a herring, if anybody bids lore). Inside is a
XVI.
         tapped barrel of ale and a cauldron full of stew, but no innkeeper to be seen. In fact, the tavern is a
         giant mimic occupied by several smaller mimics. Sleeping in the mimic tavern is a notably bad idea.

XVII.    [Random encounter] Cockatrice: A cockatrice has taken its chicks out to teach them how to hunt.

         [Random encounter] Ogre Courting Ritual: An amorous ogre is trying to impress a she-ogre with
XVIII.
         increasingly ridiculous feats of strength. They are both making a terrible racket.

         [Random encounter] Orc Hooligans: A gang of three orc youths accompanied by a random number of
XIX.     goblins are on a quest to make a name for themselves before returning to their clan. They might see the
         guild as an appropriate challenge or be convinced to join with the guild against some greater foe.

         [Random encounter] Gentle Simon: An owlbear has treed Gentle Simon of Heartsbane, a notoriously
 XX.     shrimpy sorcerer. All of Gentle Simon’s Resolve has been expended trying to rescue himself, and he’s
         now beginning to weep.


         [Quest rumor] Victims of Geralt Mourn: The adventurers find a rival guild crucified. They are still
         alive, though grievously injured and dehydrated. If the adventurers can provide aid, healing, and food,
XXI.     the rival party gasps about their recent encounter with the vampire Geralt Mourn, who the guild has
         sworn to slay. It was this dread vampire who crucified them as a warning to others. They have news of
         his current whereabouts, but would be loath to tangle with him again.

                                              No matter how accomplished an adventurer is, darkness is crippling. You

                                              Crawling in the dark is a futile pursuit. The guild is at risk of every pitfall and
                                              every trap, and creatures accustomed to darkness will find them easy prey.

                                            Whenever you fall, you may test Pentacles.

                                            • If you fail, take damage as normal.
                                            • If you succeed, treat the fall as 10’ shorter. For example, if you fall 25’
                                              and succeed in the test of Pentacles, you only suffer 1 Piercing Wound.

                                            • On a great success, treat the fall as 20’ shorter (e.g., a 25’ fall would do
                                              no damage).

                                            • On a great failure, you take damage as normal and any fragile items (like
                                              hermetic bottles) on your belt or in your pack are Destroyed.

     Example afflictions                                          Ghost lotus
     Here are some “common” afflictions to use as examples.       The seeds of the ghost lotus rewrite pathways in the
     GMs can tweak these to create any manner of gross old        user’s brain. The feeling is incredibly addictive. Habitual
     disorders for their players.                                 users of the lotus (called lotusphages) become very
                                                                  strange and otherworldly: their personalities change,
     Giant rat venom                                              their memories become distorted, and they have trouble
                                                                  distinguishing between the waking world and dreams.
     A green rat the size of a dog, covered in buboes, welts,
     and goiters, bites you. It only gets worse from there.       Stage 1: You experience euphoria. This effect cancels out

Social Encounters & Disposition
In the Underworld, you’ll encounter the bizarre denizens of the dungeons and the
adventurers trying their best to slay them (or you).

for role-playing called Disposition. Advice for GMs       circle; intense emotions are on the outside of the circle.
creating characters with interesting personalities and    Related emotions are grouped near each other.
running social encounters is provided on page 180.

100         CHAPTER 6        |   THE CRAWL PHASE
Role-playing Disposition
There are seven basic Dispositions: anger, distaste, sadness, joy, surprise, trust, and fear. Each of the seven
Dispositions are listed below, with the core emotional state of each flanked by its mild and intense states. A list of
emotional synonyms is also given, as one of those terms might be more appropriate and might aid in the GM in
appropriately role-playing the Disposition. Some notes are also given as to how a creature with that Disposition
might act in a Challenge.


Acceptance |     Trust | Admiration
Trust is a measure of belief in the general honesty,
                                                                Pensiveness |     Sadness | Grief
                                                                Sadness is emotional pain associated with loss, despair,
fairness, or capability of the other party. A base level        helplessness, or disappointment. Sad creatures often
of trust is a common starting Disposition for many              have obvious needs to be alleviated, which might change
benevolent creatures. Creatures who trust the guild will        their Disposition for the better. However, sadness often
generally negotiate in good faith, but will still cautiously    causes creatures to lose interest in activities they once
ensure the exchanges are fair. Betraying the trust of a         enjoyed, and sadness can create a significant barrier to
character is a good way to change their Disposition to          positive influences.
sad or angry.
                                                                Synonyms: anxious, empty, helpless, hopeless,
Synonyms: confident, hopeful, optimistic, playful,              depressed, irritable, guilty, lonely, abandoned
interested, inquisitive, curious
                                                                In a Challenge: In battle, those afflicted with deep
In a Challenge: Typically, creatures with this                  sadness fight with abandon. They take chances they
Disposition are not inclined to fight. If the situation         might otherwise not take. Often, they attempt to move
obligates a fight without changing the trust Disposition,       first in Initiative, recklessly charging into battle and
the creature might attempt to learn more about the              exposing themselves to danger.
guild’s prowess through non-lethal methods.

humans. Anger is one half of the fight or flight response.      life is a dirty, dirty business.

      Anxiety |   Fear | Terror
      Fear is an emotional response to a perceived danger or
                                                                  Distraction |    Surprise | Awe
                                                                  When there is a disconnect between expectations and
      threat. Fear is one half of the flight-or-fight response.   reality, a creature reacts with surprise. Surprise might
      Creatures responding with fear often want to just end       come when the guild interacts with the more “normal”

      nervous, persecuted, inferior, worried, helpless

      In a Challenge: Fearful creatures will attempt to flee      fighting today. It will fight if it believes itself threatened,
      the source of their fear, avoiding combat unless it is      but won’t pursue combat for its own purposes. It will try
      necessary to escape. They prioritize high-value cards for   to disengage as early as possible.
      their Initiative.


                                                                  Contentment |       Joy | Ecstasy
                                                                  When their needs are met, creatures feel a sense of
                                                                  joy or happiness. Like anger, feelings of joy can cloud
                                                                  judgment. This is the ideal state for influencing a
                                                                  creature, as they are well-disposed to entreaties
                                                                  and exchanges.

                                                                  Synonyms: happy, peaceful, intimate, aroused, proud,
                                                                  thankful, powerful, respected

                                                                  In a Challenge: Creatures who are joyful will not usually
                                                                  desire to engage in conflict. However, if the situation
                                                                  calls for it, joyful creatures might be cocky or overbold,
                                                                  perceiving the combat as a game. Cocky creatures might
                                                                  toy with, taunt, or tease adventurers during battle.

      The Flow of the Challenge Phase
      During the Crawl Phase, players and GMs exchange questions and answers. During
      Challenges, things become much more bounded. A Challenge narrows the lens of the
      adventure into every blow, every maneuver, every stunt that the players attempt.

      Learning the                            In this phase, everybody at the table draws cards that represent their

      Ambushes and surprise                                         Special rules
      Usually, adventurers and GM characters notice each other      As the GM sets the scene, they tell the players if
      at the same time. In remote, dark places, the existence       anything in the scene has special rules.

      TACTIC 3: SHANK THE ADVENTURERS
      The GM characters sucker punch the guild. Each
      attacker deals 1 Wound, but each individual adventurer
      can only be attacked once.

                                                                  Just a reminder:
There are also miscellaneous actions that can be
performed using any card, regardless of suit (see p. 120).        • Aces have a value of 1 (I).

The GM’s characters will also take turns over the course
of the round. During an enemy character’s turn, the GM
plays a card from their hand and adds their character’s
attribute to the total value, just like players. The GM
might have several characters that take turns over the
course of a round.

           No peeking!
           When a player declares an action that places a
           card facedown, they state what action they are
           taking, but only they know the card’s value
           until it is flipped up. Nobody but the player
           can look at the facedown card until the action
           is triggered. No peeking!

      Test Fate
      If you’re attempting a feat that seems more complex
      than a Trivial Action and has an element of chance or
      danger—like leaping a chasm, holding a door closed,
      hiding, participating in a ritual, etc.—the GM can call for
      a test of fate mid-Challenge.

      Play any card to attempt a test of fate. However, the card
      played is not counted as part of the test.

      To resolve the test of fate, draw a new card from the top
      of the minor arcana deck. The test of fate proceeds per
      the rules on page 8: You may spend Resolve for favor.
      You may push fate. You may bid your motifs.

GMing the Challenge
GMs follow slightly different rules during Challenges
                                                                                          Out of cards?
than the players.
                                                                                          If either the players or the GM must
                                                                                          draw cards but there are not enough
The basic concepts are the same: the GM acts on their turn based on their                 remaining, shuffle the discard pile
Initiative, they play cards from their hand to take actions, they use the same            and continue drawing.
actions (generally) as the players do, etc. However, it’s not practical to draw
four cards per opponent and keep track of different hands.                                This happens more frequently
                                                                                          for the GM because they draw
The major differences for the GM are explained below.                                     bigger hands of cards and the
                                                                                          major arcana deck is smaller, but


0. Set the scene
                                                                                          is a relatively rare event either way.
                                                                                          With three or four players, the Fool
                                                                                          is drawn every few rounds.
Empty rooms and deserted forest corridors make for dull combats. Create cool
spaces by filling them full of potential energy: curtains to hide behind, casks of
wine to be toppled, runaway carts to dodge, chandeliers to swing from, puddles
of oil to be lit aflame. Chapter 10: The Worm Turns has some advice for this.             Mulligans
                                                                                          Sometimes, the GM can draw all

                                                                                          legal cards to play for your Initiative
                                                                                          or actions. As a GM, you can elect
