                                                                                          greater dooms.
• +1 card for each type of enemy
                                                                                          When you mulligan, discard all
• +1 card if the enemies outnumber the adventurers                                        drawn cards and draw again.

• +1 card if there are twice as many enemies as adventurers
• +1 card for each enemy that’s physically larger than a human
• +2 cards if there is an elite enemy
• +3 cards if there is a dungeon lord
(Elite enemies and dungeon lords are defined in Appendix C: Dungeon
Denizens, page 251.)

Each of these additional cards is cumulative. Check to see which are applicable
at the start of each round. Therefore, if the number of enemies decreases, you
will draw fewer major arcana cards.

For example, if there are twelve imps facing four adventurers, the GM draws
6 cards from the major arcana deck. That includes: 3 cards to start, +1 for the
one type of enemy (imps), +1 for having more enemies than adventurers, +1 for
having twice as many enemies than adventurers.

If, over the course of the Challenge, the adventurers reduce the number of imps
to seven, the GM will draw 5 cards at the beginning of the next round: 3 + 1 for
having one enemy type (imps) and +1 for having more enemies than adventurers.

                                             Lesser dooms
                                             Lesser doom cards have values of 1–14. These are analogous to the minor arcana
                                             (which are also rated from 1–14).

                                             Play any lesser doom card to make any Challenge Action (Attack, Dash,
                                             Dodge, etc.). Only add the enemy’s attributes to the action’s value on their
                                             turn, as normal.

                                             You also play a lesser doom card to use an enemy’s lesser doom abilities. These
                                             are special powers or tactics unique to that creature.

Tracking enemy damage                                                                 Weapon properties
                                                                                      Each type of weapon has a special
As the GM tracks the status of several combatants, they track Wounds in a             property that changes the way you
simplified way. Each enemy has a Health and Defense (HD) rating.                      use it in combat. See page 170 for a
                                                                                      list of special weapon properties.
Health represents a creature’s ability to absorb damage. For example, a giant
can shrug off many small stings from puny humans. A skeleton has no vitals and
must be bashed apart before it stops moving.
                                                                                      Taking the murder
Defense represents a creature’s ability to deflect damage. For example, the           out of murder-hobo
plate armor of a death knight or the overlapping scales of a dragon.                  If someone is taken down by an
                                                                                      Attack, the person striking the
A creature with 3 Health and 5 Defense would be rendered like so: HD: 3/5             finishing blow can elect to spare
                                                                                      their life, disabling, knocking out,
As a GM’s character is Wounded, the GM reduces either its Health or                   or subduing their enemy, per the
Defense points.                                                                       GM’s discretion.

• Reduce the enemy’s Defense first.
• When there’s no Defense left, reduce the enemy’s Health.
• Piercing attacks bypass Defense and always reduce Health.
• When an enemy reaches 0 Health, they are at Death’s Door.
  • Some creatures bypass Death’s Door and are simply destroyed. For
    example, neither a clockwork statue nor a zombie are living and would
    simply fall apart.

This song is usually called the “Camping Song,” and it’s sung to an ancient melody. The Camping Song runs thus:

                                                                             CHAPTER 8       |   THE CAMP PHASE   135
      The Flow of the Camp Phase
      When adventuring has left the guild injured, miserable, and expended, they put down
      their packs and set up camp. During the Camp Phase, everyone rests and recovers from the
      stresses of the Crawl.

      The Camp Phase runs thus:

      1. Camp Actions
      Set up camp and perform a Camp Action.


      2. Break bread
      Consume a ration. If you can't do this, check the
      Stressed condition.


      3. No rest for the wicked
      The GM checks for any random Camp events.


      4. Recovery
      Automatically refill your allotment of lore bids and clear
      the Staggered condition. For every charged Bond you
      burn, heal 1 Wound or regain 1 point of Resolve.

      • If you are Stressed, you must burn a charged Bond to
        erase this condition first. Being Stressed prevents you
        from healing Wounds or recovering Resolve.

      • If you are Injured, you must burn a Bond to clear this
        condition before you can heal any Wounded talents.


      5. End of Camp Phase
      Check to make sure you have at least two of the
      following: bedroll, tent, or fire. If you don’t, you wake
      up Stressed.




          The pace of travel
          Rations are the resource that drive the Camp
          Phase. As such, the opportunity to perform
          Camp Actions is dependent on the guild’s
          ability to manage their inventory. Likewise,
          because charged Bonds drive step 4 of the
          Camp Phase (Recovery), you have an impetus to
          avoid striking camp too often: only after a good
          exchange of role-playing scenes.

Update Maps
Spend some time updating your map and charting your
course. Mark down the rooms that you’ve traveled
through since your last Camp Phase. These are your
mapped rooms.

You can travel through two mapped rooms per watch.
This allows you to travel through two mapped rooms per
Meatgrinder event instead of one.

                                            3. No rest for the wicked
      starving, skip steps 4 and 5 of the
      Camp Phase. You cannot burn
      charged Bonds or regain lore bids
      while starving.                       While the adventurers rest, the Underworld continues to go about its sinister
                                            business. The GM should draw on the Meatgrinder table for the dungeon
                                            the adventurers are camping in (p. 91). Random events like rainstorms and rising
                                            fog will add flavor to the Camp Phase, but probably won’t impose any special
                                            rules. If a random encounter is pulled, the Camp Phase is interrupted
                                            by a Challenge.

                                            It is assumed that adventurers are taking turns guarding the camp while they
                                            rest. If a random encounter occurs, the GM should randomly determine who’s
                                            on watch. An easy way to do this is to look at the top card of the minor arcana
                                            discard pile: the suit displayed corresponds to the path of the adventurer on
                                            guard. If there are multiple adventurers of the same path, odd cards target the
                                            player to the GM’s left, even cards target the player to the GM’s right.

                                            The adventurer on guard tests Cups.

                                            • If successful, the alarm is raised before the random encounter finds the
                                              encampment. The guild has a brief period of time to prepare.

                                            • If the test of fate is a failure, the guild is surprised.
                                              • A guild caught asleep is very vulnerable—nobody is wearing armor or
                                                actively wielding weapons.

                                              • See page 110 for the rules about surprise.

                                            If one of the players has performed the Patrol action, the GM draws twice
                                            on the Meatgrinder table and chooses a non-encounter result if possible.
                                            A Challenge only occurs if both cards reveal a random encounter—the GM
                                            chooses which one to use.

                                            Once the Challenge is resolved, the Camp Phase continues on to step 4.

      Optional Rules:

      Overland Travel
      Most of His Majesty the Worm is focused on dungeon-crawling in the mythic
      Underworld. It abstracts concerns of food, time, and distance into the flow of
      the Camp and Crawl Phases. If your game takes place in a setting where the sun shines,
      you might want a system that adds an additional layer of logistics to travel. If this is the
      case, use these rules.


      Each day is divided into three watches. Each watch takes
      about eight hours.                                          Overland actions
                                                                  Each watch, the guild can perform one of the following
      Using these optional rules, timekeeping becomes             overland actions. It’s important to note that, using these
      important. After three watches, a new day dawns. The        optional rules, step 1 of the Camp Phase is separated
      GM should step through the calendar as they pass day        from steps 2–5.
      by day.

      For each watch, follow this procedure:                      Camp Action

      1. Choose action                                            listed on pages 137–139 to perform.

      The guild chooses a single overland action to take.
                                                                  Encamp
      2. Meatgrinder                                              The guild beds down for the night. Run through steps
                                                                  2–5 of the Camp Phase.
      The GM draws on their Meatgrinder table for a random
      event or encounter.
                                                                  Explore
      3. Set the scene                                            Look for interesting things within a hex. The GM
                                                                  informs the guild of any notable features, lairs, terrain,
      The GM describes the random encounter in the context        or spoor that are discoverable within the area they’re in.
      of the hex the guild is traveling in. The players and the
      GM play out the scene, and when it’s over, the GM calls
      for a new overland action to be chosen.                     Interact

                                                                  a dungeon or visiting a hamlet).


                                                                  Travel
      “The cave you fear to enter holds                           The guild travels from their current hex into an adjacent

           the treasure you seek.”                                everyone in the guild is riding, they can move another

                                                                  hunger come into play more than under the standard
                                                                  rules. Characters who fail to Encamp once per day
                                                                  become Exhausted—all tests and all Challenge Actions

“Of that Byzantine Empire, the universal verdict of history is that it constitutes, with
   scarcely an exception, the most thoroughly base and despicable form that civilisation
  has yet assumed. . . They possessed knowledge; they had continually before them the noble
   literature of ancient Greece, instinct with the loftiest heroism; but that literature,
  which afterwards did so much to revivify Europe, could fire the degenerate Greeks with
no spark or semblance of nobility. The history of the Empire is a monotonous story of the
          intrigues of priests, eunuchs, and women, of poisonings, of conspiracies,

                                                                           CHAPTER 9        |   THE CITY PHASE              147
      The Flow of the City Phase
      When the guild returns to civilization, laden with treasure and light on supplies, the City
      Phase begins. The City Phase is an opportunity to pursue long-term goals, research the
      next steps of the quest, and restock supplies before returning to the Stygian depths. This
      chapter details what players need to know about the City Phase. Advice for the GM for
      running the City Phase is found on page 190. Procedures for the GM to flesh out a City
      are found in Appendix D: City Creation.

      Here is the summary of the City Phase:

      1. Death and taxes                                         5. Upkeep

      3. City Events
      The City is never dull. When you stagger back to the         Rumors (XI–XV): Rumors hint at the contents of the
      surface, you enter a chaotic metropolis with all its         Underworld: treasures, monsters, traps, hazards, and
      intrigues, politics, and spectacle.                          history. Rumors are opportunities to tell lore and define
                                                                   the “story” of the dungeon.
      Before play, the GM should construct a City Events
      table, detailing potential events that frame the guild’s     Travel events (XVI–XX): Travel events are often things
      visit. During this step, the GM draws a major arcana         that go wrong in a trip to the City, or a chance to
      card, consults this table, and interprets the result.        confront the players to make a hard choice.

      The results need not happen instantly. For example, if       Signs and Portents (XXI): Signs and portents are special
      the GM draws a rumor on the City Events table, they          events wherein weirdness has spilled out from the
      might have a contract-giver or shopkeeper deliver the        Underworld and complicates life in the City. When
      rumor to the guild through the course of playing out the     drawing this result, the GM looks at the top card of the
      City Phase.                                                  minor arcana discard pile and then consults the Signs and
                                                                   Portents table (p. 153).
      The City Events table should have twenty-one entries
      and follow this formula:
                                                                                          Like the Meatgrinder table, the
      Curiosities (I–V): Curiosities are moments of serendipity.                          GM should keep the City Events
      GMs, use these events to inject color into the                                      table tidy and fresh, swapping
      game. Curiosities create a sense of realness, and are                               out used entries with new content
      opportunities to demonstrate what kind of City exists                               (see step 8 on p. 160).
      in your game. Are curiosity events dark portents like
      raving madmen calling for repentance under the blood
      moon or are they bucolic affairs with Punch and Judy                                The next page has an example
      puppet shows?                                                                       City Events table to serve as a
                                                                                          starting point.
      Happenings (VI–X): Happenings are
      events that frame the lives of the
      residents of the City. These are
      the saturnalia, feasts, and holy days
      that break up the wheel of years.
      Happenings should make the City
      Phase feel different to the players.

      Visiting the City during a
      religious festival
      is much different
      than visiting
      during the normal
      drudge of days.




150        CHAPTER 9        |   THE CITY PHASE
Example City Events
Card City Event
  I.     [Curiosity] Gross: A bucket of night soil is emptied onto a random adventurer from a high-up window.

         [Curiosity] Doggy: A starving dog trails behind the guild, whining. Its ribs stick out and its pink skin
  II.    is clearly visible through its mangy fur. It licks your hands with a dry, grey tongue. If you feed it, it may
         follow you.

         [Curiosity] An Execution: A crowd gathers to watch a hanging. A tonsured Mythric cultist of middling
 III.    initiation pronounces a sentence of death on a hooded man for the crime of punching a noble and
         subsequently loosening the noble’s tooth. To loud applause, the man drops and jerks on the gibbet.

         [Curiosity] Stylite: From his high pillar, a naked stylite pronounces doom down on the adventurer
         with the highest Wands score. The stylite loudly decries their vices and denounces their escapades
  IV.
         as lecherous and murderous. He seems to know a lot about the adventurer, honestly. It would be
         impressive if it wasn’t so mean and truthful.

         [Curiosity] Lick Lick Lick: An old woman, drunk as a skunk, sits in the gutter singing an old-
  V.
         fashioned tune. She doesn’t seem to notice the bloated rat licking her ankles.

         [Happening] Famine: A long winter has left the granaries empty. Food is scarce. You can only buy
 VI.
         rations if you maintain a luxurious lifestyle during step 5 (Upkeep).

         [Happening] The Ecstasy of St. Naos: By far the biggest party day of the year: like St. Patrick’s and
 VII.    Mardi Gras had a baby. The City is shut down. The only City Action the adventurers can perform
         during step 6 (City Actions) is Carousing.

         [Happening] The Coronation of Maiden Wisdom: One of the highest holy days in the Mythric
 VIII.   calendar, charity is given generously during this time. Rates for upkeep are reduced: impoverished is
         15g, common is 25g, and luxurious is 50g.

         [Happening] The Feast of the Constellations: During the Feast of the Constellations, the pious of the
 IX.     Cult fast. By custom and law, all taverns are closed and the drinking of alcohol is punished by use of a
         scold’s bridle. Carousing cannot be performed during this phase.

         [Happening] The King is Dead, Long Live the King!: The old ruler is gone (assassinated? death
  X.     faked? exiled?). The GM must determine who now sits the throne over the City. The players should
         expect changes from the new regime.


         [Rumor] The Sporehulk’s Wife: The Sporehulk is the dungeon lord of the Sepulcher. It is said that
         inside one of the chambers lies the barrow of his wife, around which is arranged four canopic jars
 XI.
         containing her brains, her liver, her lungs, and her ovaries. If you eat any part of the Sporehulk’s wife,
         it’s said you’ll undergo a terrible and awesome transformation.




                                                                          CHAPTER 9        |   THE CITY PHASE            151
      Card City Event
               [Rumor] The Star’s Daughter: A fallen star dwells on an island in the Boundless Moat, and his
               daughter came with him into exile. Both star-beings struggle adorably with human culture. The star
       XII.    wishes for someone to marry his daughter. As a dowry, the star will grant a wish to anybody who marries
               her. However, the daughter will interpret the wish. It would be wise to keep her happy unless you want
               the wish to go sour.

               [Rumor] Medusa’s Abortion: A gorgon was recently slain in the Underworld, yet somehow its
               premature fetus survived. The awful, crawling, half-serpentine thing is gnawing its way through the
      XIII.
               Castle of Crossed Destinies. Even glancing at it turns you into stone. That’s why there are so many
               more statues in the Castle as of late.

               [Rumor] The Strangler’s Palm: Inside a hidden room in the Castle of Crossed Destinies is a tavern—a
               haven for adventurers in the middle of the Worm’s own realm. If you can find it, 10g will purchase a
      XIV.
               safe place to encamp and some of the most exotic foods you’ve ever eaten. The password this month is
               “pickle juice.”

               [Rumor] The Tomb of the First Dead: Inside the City of Ruin is a graveyard. The first graveyard,
               in fact. It is called the Tomb of the First Dead, and it holds a mausoleum for the first human to ever
       XV.
               succumb to the doom of old age and death. Inside this tomb is a treasure that will make you immune to
               the mental control of the three immortal nymphs that live within the Underworld.


               [Travel event] A Theft: The adventurer in back of the marching order is bumped into by a louse-
      XVI.     ridden orphan. Later, as they round a corner, they see a piece of gear that looks suspiciously like their
               own at a merchant’s stall. Several interested buyers are already taking notice.


               [Travel event] A Challenge: A pair of bravos sitting outside of a wine sink make snide remarks about
      XVII.    the clothes of the adventurer with the highest Pentacles score. They’re spoiling for a fight, though
               they’re more into humiliation than actual harm.


               [Travel event] A Proposition: Several whores call down compliments about the adventurer with the
      XVIII.
               highest Wands score. They claim they’ll give them a discount, if the adventurer is so inclined.


               [Travel event] An Inheritance: The adventurer with the lowest Cups score receives a letter from their
               family. A distant uncle has died and bequeathed them a townhouse by the Grey River, complete with
      XIX.
               a snooty butler named Aethelred that hates them. Though initially a boon, this townhouse will soon
               become the center of a web of intrigue that will haunt the guild.


               [Travel event] A Disaster: Fire! After step 6 (City Actions), the inn the guild is staying at catches fire.
       XX.     This prompts a test of Pentacles to escape quickly. If anybody fails, they leave behind the two items in
               the very bottom of their pack and begin the next Crawl with the Stressed condition.


               [Signs and Portents] Strange Days: The GM notes the top card on the minor arcana discard pile and
      XXI.
               describes something from the Signs and Portents table (facing page).

      Because His Majesty the Worm             you which merchant can craft it for you.
      abstracts pricing lists into upkeep,
      it can be hard to know what a “fair”   • Describe it in a few words. The price for a commissioned craft is as follows:
      price is for a specific item.
                                               • 1 gold per syllable of the commission if it’s something a farmer might
      Don’t think like that: no price is         have. Examples: scrimshaw pipe (3g), tricorn hat (3g), pan flute (2g),
      fair. The cutthroat, mercantile City       wooden dentures (4g)
      is a slave to capricious capitalism.
      The “syllable method” is an easy         • 5 gold per syllable of the commission if it’s something an adventurer might
      way to adjudicate prices that range        have. Examples: helmet with a candle holder (40g), imp trap (10g), silver-
      from the simple to the complex.            thread bug net (25g)

      If you have something like a             • 10 gold per syllable of the commission if it’s something a noble might have.
      merchant in the Underworld (a              Examples: mirror masquerade mask (60g), cloth of gold gown (40g), lion-
      sentient crawfish that sells exotic        themed parade armor (70g), bespoke clothing (40g)
      meats? an undead blacksmith who
      sells scavenged grave goods?), you       • 25 gold per syllable of the commission if it’s something that nobody has—

      down there, too.                           (125g), decorative harpy wings (175g)

                                             The fewer details you provide, the more details the GM will supplement. If you
                                             have a clear picture in mind, articulate what you want using the name of the
                                             item. No fair saying you want a “set of ten-foot mechanical articulate tongs”
                                             by just saying “Long tongs.”

                                             “Reasonableness” is up to the GM. We don’t really truck with steampunk
                                             machinery or firearms or whatever, but maybe your table is different.

                                             Assuming that the adventurer has an appropriate motif that establishes them
                                             as a craftsman, the adventurer can be the one actually making the item. The
                                             prices are the same: the gold is spent on renting a workshop and supplying
                                             raw materials.

Train
Seek out an expert and study under them. Talk to the GM about what talent
you want to learn. The GM will tell you who is available to train you.

• Spend 50 gold per 1XP you want to invest on the new talent.
• Prepare as many uses of that talent as you have XP invested.
• See page 33 for full details about training talents.

      Advice for Exploration-

      “The adventure is in the wilderness,    Once every player has resolved their City Action, the GM sets a role-playing
      not the town. As per the discussion     scene in a tavern where the guild comes together to debrief, drink, and
      of NPCs [non-player characters]         determine their next steps.

      focus to urban adventure instead        Taverns have job boards where contracts are offered to guilds. These are
      of exploration. You can have as         jobs that characters in the City offer to guilds, with rewards of coin, peerage,

                                              8. Restock the Underworld
                                              The Underworld grows and shifts. Between the end of the City Phase and the
                                              start of the next session, the GM revisits their Meatgrinder and City Events
                                              tables and replaces any entries that the players have already encountered. If an
                                              ogre is slain, a hidden room looted, or a rusty trap sprung, replace those entries
                                              with something new.

                                              GMs should ask themselves:
                                              How has the Underworld been
                                              changed by the player’s actions?
                                              Factions will refill their posts.
                                              Other factions will move
                                              into cleared rooms. Other
                                              guilds meet with success or
                                              failure. The Underworld is
                                              dynamic, not static. Reflect
                                              the changing Underworld
                                              by adding new content to the
                                              Meatgrinder tables.

                                                                            CHAPTER 9       |   THE CITY PHASE            161
      The Omphalic Market
      No tale tells what ancient power minted the ubiquitous star-marked golden coins that
      sit in the treasure hoards of the Underworld. But all know that these coins have become
      the de facto standard of the City. Coinages of lesser metals have become worthless. As
      guilds have hauled back vast quantities of glittering gold, merchants of the great Omphalic
      Market will only accept Underworld gold as payment.




       “In the Plaza of Dark Delights, which lies seven blocks south of the Marsh Gate
         and extends from the Fountain of Dark Abundance to the Shrine of the Black
        Virgin, the shop-lights glinted upward no more brightly than the stars glinted down.
          For there the vendors of drugs and the peddlers of curiosa and the hawkers of
         assignations light their stalls and crouching places with foxfire, glowworms, and
                 fire-pots with tiny single windows, and they conduct their business
                            almost as silently as the stars conduct theirs.”
                                     – “Bazaar of the Bizarre,” Franz Leiber


162       CHAPTER 9   |   THE CITY PHASE
Buying new gear
During step 5 of the City Phase (Upkeep), you determine what you purchase for your next adventure. These prices are
abstracted. You don’t tally your money for each torch, each ration, or each dagger. Rather, you fill your pack—as much
as it can hold—based on your upkeep level (or lower): impoverished, common, or luxurious.

164        CHAPTER 9        |   THE CITY PHASE
CHAPTER 9   |   THE CITY PHASE   165
                                Candle
                                Candles provide bright light for the person carrying them, but don’t provide
                                any light for those nearby. As such, they are used when the guild—as a whole—
                                prefers stealth. Candles can be snuffed out and relit (whereas torches cannot
                                be). Candles go out when dropped. Candles can flicker 2 times before they’re
                                used up (p. 95).


                                Chain
                                Chain comes in 10’ lengths per slot. Chain is useful for all sorts of bindings
                                and haulings.


                                Chalk
                                Chalk can make marks almost anywhere—useful for plotting your way around
                                a maze, warning fellow adventurers about traps, or making crude drawings of
                                your rivals’ mothers.


                                Clothes
                                Clothes come in several varieties.

                                • Rags preserve your basic dignity, but make you look like the worst sort of
                                  peasant.

                                • Common clothes won’t make you popular at parties, but they’re serviceable
                                  and good for dirty work.

                                • Finery sets you apart from the general rabble. Be careful, though;
                                  adventuring has a tendency to make you dirty and bloody.

                                The clothes that you’re wearing aren’t in your pack and don’t take up any slots.
                                Spare sets of clothes take 1 slot in your pack.


                                Cooking gear
                                Cooking gear is needed to prepare hunted game into edible food during the
                                Camp Phase.


                                Crowbar
                                Crowbars are used to pry open doors and chests by testing Swords. Less subtle
                                than a lockpick, doing so breaks the door in question.


                                Falconry gear
                                Falconry gear includes gloves, tethers, hoods, and everything needed to enjoy
                                the royal sport of hawking.


                                Fishing gear
                                Fishing gear is needed to fish and gather food on bodies of water—like in the
                                deadly Boundless Moat.

168         CHAPTER 9       |   THE CITY PHASE
Torch
Torches provide bright light to the person holding them and dim light
for everybody else in the guild. Torches have a 50% chance to go out when
dropped. Torches that are extinguished are almost impossible to relight.
Torches can flicker 3 times before they’re used up (p. 95).


Wand of archwood
Wands of archwood are ritual implements that allow sorcerers to focus their
magical potential. If you have the Gramarye talent (p. 82), you may use an
archwood wand as a missile weapon to create blasts of magical energy up to a
zone away.


Weaponry
Weaponry includes any basic arms and ammo listed in the Weapons section on
the following page.

• Silver weaponry is expensive, but silver is often useful against lycanthropes,
  spirits, and certain types of undead. Silver weaponry is soft and easily damaged,
  however. Silver weapons can only absorb 1 Notch before being Destroyed.


Wolfsbane
Wolfsbane repels wolves and lycanthropes. If brandished, test Wands. If
successful, Displace one affected creature. During a Challenge, brandishing
wolfsbane is a Wands action.




 “To train with the sword, first master sweeping. When you have
 mastered sweeping, you must master the way of drawing water.
Once you have learned how to draw water, you must split wood.
Once you have split wood, you must learn the arts of finding the
  fine herbs in the forest, the arts of writing, the arts of paper
making, and poetry writing. You must become familiar with the
 awl and the pen in equal measure. When you have mastered all
  these things you must master building a house. Once your house
is built, you have no further need for a sword, since it is an ugly
              piece of metal and its adherents idiots.”
                – Kill Six Billion Demons, Tom Parkinson-Morgan

172         CHAPTER 9         |   THE CITY PHASE
Alisander chooses the spells Brainfever, Control Undead,
and Necromancy. He writes these components down on his
adventurer sheet, with each component taking a slot.

Step 7. Plan the next Crawl
GM: OK, so everybody has their actions done. Uh, let’s
see. You all meet back up at a tavern. Do you want to go
back to the Rat Cellar?

Weela: Ha ha, yes yes.

GM: OK, you descend the familiar crumbling stairs down
into the basement bar. You get your cups and pull yourself
a draft of the terrible, licorice-smelling liquor called rat’s
milk. The same unsavory characters as always are there—
arm wrestling, getting in spitting contests. There’s a job
board in the corner. A big rat is gnawing on the cork of
the board. What do you all do?

Lucind: I go over, try and pet the rat, then read the
job board.

The GM has pre-constructed a table of contracts. They draw 5
cards and read the corresponding contracts to the guild.

The guild role-plays together. None of the contracts sound
particularly appetizing to them for one reason or another. They
did not complete Alisander’s quest last Crawl, so they will
continue pursuing that goal. They briefly discuss what they
think their leads are. The guild decides to try to go towards the
Sepulcher of Titans dungeon.

Step 8. Restock the Underworld
After the session, the GM opens up their notes document and
goes into their random tables—specifically, their Meatgrinder
table and their City Events table.

They delete the entries on the Meatgrinder table that have been
drawn. After thinking a little about how the factions in the
Underworld have changed because of the guild’s actions, they
write some new Meatgrinder entries.

They delete the old City Event rumor about the star-daughter.
They write a new rumor based on the Meatgrinder entries they
just wrote.

The GM looks over their maps and makes sure they’re all
up to date.

In general, the GM doesn’t create new “plot.” They
just think about the environment and make notes about
potentially interesting consequences that could arise from
the adventurers’ actions.

      The GM’s Manifesto
      A game is all about decisions. That is essentially what every game is, whether it's a
      traditional game like poker, or a board game, or an RPG.

      A role-playing game’s play happens via discussion. The
      GM describes things, the players ask questions, the GM       Create engaging personas
      elaborates, the players describe things, the GM asks         The Underworld and the City should both be full
      questions, the players elaborate, and the process repeats.   of memorable characters with their own interesting
      It’s a back-and-forth—asking questions and answering         motivations. Each of the GM’s characters has a
      them. During this exchange, the GM and the players           personality defined by their likes, dislikes, wants, and
      make decisions. This is what’s fun about RPGs.               needs.

      Therefore, your job is to create interesting decisions for   In the same way that dangers should be broadcast, so
      the players. Some advice to this end:                        should your characters’ personalities. By clearly showing
                                                                   what a character’s likes and dislikes are, players will be
      • Create environments that incite interesting decisions      given opportunities to role-play meaningfully.

      • Create characters and factions with interesting            The Underworld is deadly enough that not every single
        motivations                                                denizen needs to be hostile. The Disposition rules
                                                                   (p. 99) make sure that players have a fair shake when
      • Describe the environment fully, engaging sight,            encountering new characters. Give players opportunities
        hearing, smell, taste, and touch                           to gather information, make unlikely allies, and take part
                                                                   in factional intrigue.
      • Act in good faith by speaking generously
      • Referee player actions fairly                              Engage the senses
                                                                   Meaningful exploration only works when the players
      Create meaningful exploration                                have a good sense of what is going on. Players need
                                                                   you to tell them as much information as possible about
      Decisions in an RPG should be interesting, not               the environment they are acting within. Paint pictures
      arbitrary. It is essential that, during the Crawl, you       with your descriptions, actually sketch out rooms when
      provide meaningful choices so that exploration is both       mental pictures are difficult to conjure, and be vivid
      fun and engaging.                                            about all five senses. Don’t leave out any salient details
                                                                   about things that players can see, hear, feel, or smell.

      Creating interesting characters
      It’s your job to portray characters with personalities that are evocative, strange,
      conflicting, and clearly broadcast. This is true for all creatures that you control,
      no matter how monstrous!


      Each character you introduce should have a personality           Wants
      defined by their dislikes and likes, wants and needs.            Wants fulfill the character’s wishes.

      • Dislikes are gates to the character’s heart.                   • Wants are discrete. They can be items (“enough money
                                                                         for a dowry”) or events (“marry the widow Prescott”).
      • Likes are the key.
                                                                       • If a GM character is offered something they want as a
      • Wants are aspirational character desires.                        bargaining chip, tests of fate to manipulate them are
                                                                         made with favor.
      • Needs are foundational character desires.
                                                                       Needs
      Understanding a character’s personality allows you               Needs represent the status quo.
      to arbitrate the guild’s attempts to bargain with them
      fairly. Reference the Dispositions on page 99 for role-          • Needs are abstract and essential (“for Baron Afanas
      playing guidance.                                                  to stay in power so the peasants continue to pay their
                                                                         taxes to me”).
      Dislikes
      Dislikes trigger negative Dispositions like distaste or anger.   • If a GM character’s needs are threatened as a
                                                                         bargaining chip, tests of Wands to manipulate them are
      • These triggers can be behaviors (“lying”) or traits              made with favor but their Disposition will be a hostile
        (“all elves”).                                                   one, such as anger or distaste. They won’t bargain
                                                                         again.
      • GM characters won’t bargain with adventurers that
        they dislike.                                                  Contrasting or conflicting likes, dislikes, wants, and
                                                                       needs ensures that the players have multiple ways to
      Likes                                                            interact with GM characters.
      Likes trigger positive Dispositions like trust or joy.
                                                                       For instance, some mermaids might like gossip and
      • These triggers can be behaviors (“sharing alcohol”) or         want to eat a man’s eyes, the tips of his fingers, and his
        traits (“good at music”).                                      privates. A guild of men encountering mermaids are
                                                                       likely targets to be devoured. However, if the guild feed
      • GM characters will bargain fairly with adventurers that        the mermaids juicy gossip instead, they might avoid a
        they like.                                                     combat encounter.

What can I see?                                               What do I know?
When a player asks what their adventurer can see,             When a player asks, “Would my character know about
describe everything in the room that they could possibly      X?” make a quick call on how obscure the question is.
see or notice. This gives players enough context to           If the question is something their adventurer might
actually interact with the room in a meaningful way.          possibly know, speak generously about the subject. If the
                                                              question is obscure, ask the player if they have a motif
This information is filtered by a few factors, of course.     they could use to bid lore (p. 32).
An adventurer might not be able to see in the dark, but
they could still hear their environment. They won't be        There are essentially two levels of knowledge.
able to see hidden or obscured objects (like a secret door
or a thief hiding behind a curtain), but are free to search   1. Obvious knowledge: This covers stuff everybody
in more thorough ways.                                           knows and sets the general expectations of a situation.
                                                                 Giving players a lot of information makes sure that
Essentially, there are three levels of information based         both players and the GM are on the same page and lets
on how thoroughly an adventurer looks around them.               players make intelligent choices.
No tests are required and no cards need to be drawn;
the only thing that is tested is a player’s thoughtfulness    2. Obscure knowledge: Some specialist subjects are
while asking questions.                                          only going to be known to certain people. Obscure
                                                                 knowledge might include the habits of supernatural
1. Glancing: This covers everything that can be perceived        creatures, the likes and dislikes of specific people
   in an area by someone who has good light.                     within an organization, or the metaphysics of the
                                                                 planes of reality. This information should only be
2. Scrutinizing: Gated, until the players ask questions.         given to players who bid lore.
   “Is the gargoyle made of stone?” “What color is the
   book?” “What are the pages made out of?” “Are the          If a player bids lore and you accept the question, give as
   hinges inside or out?”                                     much information on the subject as you know—just keep
                                                              talking and riffing until you run out of material.
3. Investigatory: Gated, until the adventurers interact
   with the environment. “I try to twist the moose head.
   Does it feel like it has any give?” “I’ll pull back the
   tapestry. Is there anything behind it?” “I tap on the
   walls. Do they sound hollow?”

Information should only rarely be held back from the
players. Be charitable in the information you give: the
more information a player has, the more interesting
choices they can make. So, even in a room with a secret
door, the adventurer might feel a slight draft in the room
that reveals that something is amiss. Or if there was a
thief behind a curtain, they might hear a muffled cough
for a moment, but then nothing.

184         CHAPTER 10       |   THE WORM TURNS: GAMEMASTERING
Creating interesting battles
Your job as the GM is to keep the Challenge flowing. You track the Initiative
count, lead discussions about rules, and make rule calls when players attempt
different types of actions. And, importantly, you control the antagonists during
the Challenge.

Here are some lessons learned during playtesting to help you create tactically
difficult and rewarding Challenges.


Gang up on the players
Players have more cards in total than the GM. They will act more often.
However, you have an advantage when it comes to the number of antagonists.

• With multiple enemies, each action you use can target the same number of
  adventurers. If five goblins use the Attack action, this will affect up to five
  different adventurers.

  • Enemies can also focus fire, attacking the same adventurer. Use the rules
    for mobs on page 122 to good effect.

• The GM’s “side” can often absorb more Wounds than the players.
The gimmick is that players feel cool as they mow down hordes of zombies or
bandits or whatever. At the same time, it’s a war of attrition—the GM can put
pressure on the players as they face hordes of enemies.


Make minor actions as often as possible
You have much more freedom than players when it comes to card choice
because you don’t have to worry about card suits. As such, take minor actions as
often as possible.

Smart players will try to keep the monsters “stun-locked” with Roughhouse
and various effects. Smart GMs will use Recover, which doesn’t have a requisite
value—simply discard any lesser doom card as a minor action to keep your
antagonists free and ready to act.


Fight dirty, fight fair
Don’t pull punches, but fight fair. Don’t change your monsters’ stats halfway
through a battle. If the players come up with an amazing plan and shove your
big bad guy off of a tower, let it happen. Of course, what is good for the goose
is good for the gander. If the players start shoving your Balrog off the Bridge
of Khazad-dûm, you can pull their wizard off of it just as easily (if you have the
appropriate card).

If the players are losing, they have a choice to make: stand and fight, run away,
or talk their way out of it. The Disposition and Morale rules make sure that the
players have ample opportunities to talk their way out of a fight at pretty much
any stage.




                                                    CHAPTER 10        |   THE WORM TURNS: GAMEMASTERING   185
      Creating interesting antagonists
      Challenges that just consist of “smack the other guy dead” can be boring. Make
      fights with goals other than defeating the enemy. To this end, create antagonists with
      potential energy.

      For example, if a Meatgrinder encounter simply lists “1–4 skeletons,” the Challenge
      Phase will consist of the antagonists whacking each other until one side expires from
      Wounds. However, if the Meatgrinder details, “1–4 skeletons in a pit that seem to be
      guarding a skeleton with a golden crown; the crowned skeleton is not moving,” the
      encounter gains more texture and raises several questions:

      • Can the adventurers get the crown off of the king skeleton safely?
        • What happens if they do? Does this trigger something?

      • What is the story of these undead? How does it
        relate to this region of the Underworld?

      • How can the pit be safely navigated by the
        adventurers?

      As the guild moves through the Underworld,
      the potential energy from one antagonist
      will transfer onto another until eventually
      there is an explosion—with the players
      caught in the middle.




186        CHAPTER 10       |   THE WORM TURNS: GAMEMASTERING
Creating surprises
If things are beginning to get stagnant, introduce something that changes the Challenge dramatically. Let the
potential energy transfer into kinetic energy.

Here’s a table to inspire ideas for different ways to shake things up. Glance at the top of the minor arcana discard pile
for a random event:



   Card Twist
            The current conflict smashes down a nearby wall, connecting the current room to an adjacent one.

    III     An infantile wandering monster wanders into the scene. It imprints onto a random adventurer.

     IV     A rival adventuring party, currently struggling with problems of their own, crash onto the scene.

     V      Something in the current scene is revealed to only be an illusion.

            Something in the scene is revealed, with further investigation, to be something completely different.
     VI
            The orc is just three goblins in a trench coat. The gargoyle is just a statue.

    VII     A secret passage is revealed, leading to hidden treasure or danger.

      darkness; a time for the whole table to breathe a sigh of relief.

      Running the City Phase
      Social encounters in the City aren’t like social encounters in the Underworld. In the
      Underworld, the characters are invaders. In the City, characters are part of the ecosystem.
      That is a fundamentally different paradigm.

      Through role-playing, the City blooms for the players. However, the players must find
      the appropriate keys for the gates that are placed in front of them. The GM’s job is
      threefold: Find what goals the players have, clearly define what is needed to achieve those
      goals, and create interesting obstacles.


      Seed and grow goals Create a path to success

      web of intrigue that makes the City Phase especially            a player can declare a clear goal, you can provide a clear
      interesting. This is done by clearly showing the                path towards that goal.
      resources, boons, and wish fulfillment that can be gained
      by interacting with the City factions.                          The Support City Action (p. 159) is the main tool that

      Spine of Night
      Although it’s not about dungeon crawling, the sheer          Ultimately, this novel is one of the finest examples of
      inventiveness of its ultra-gory, heavy-metal aesthetic       fantasy fiction in the English language.
      is hard to rival. It deals with brutal warriors, greedy
      scholars, winged assassins, and power-mad sorcerers
      delving into powers that mortals were not meant to
      know. Watch it and be inspired.
